<div id="review_712729305" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/712729305" />
    <a title="Rachel Hamilton" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/20086072-rachel-hamilton"><img alt="Rachel Hamilton" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1442966984p2/20086072.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/712729305?book_show_action=true">Sep 05, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Rachel Hamilton" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Rachel Hamilton" href="/user/show/20086072-rachel-hamilton">Rachel Hamilton</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer712729305" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12468357608434540465">Star rating: * * * * * 5 out of 5<br/><br/>Oof! Just finished <i>Last Stand of Dead Men</i> and I feel like I’ve been fighting alongside Skulduggery, Valkyrie, Tanith and the rest for the last few days. When Derek Landy says on the cover, ‘No one is safe’, you’d better believe it. The book offers everything you’d expect from the eighth installment in the Skulduggery Pleasant series: action, action and more action, with the usual witty one-liners and spiky dialogue thrown in to the horror – slash – comedy – slash</span>
  <span id="freeText12468357608434540465" style="display:none">Star rating: * * * * * 5 out of 5<br /><br />Oof! Just finished <i>Last Stand of Dead Men</i> and I feel like I’ve been fighting alongside Skulduggery, Valkyrie, Tanith and the rest for the last few days. When Derek Landy says on the cover, ‘No one is safe’, you’d better believe it. The book offers everything you’d expect from the eighth installment in the Skulduggery Pleasant series: action, action and more action, with the usual witty one-liners and spiky dialogue thrown in to the horror – slash – comedy – slash – adventure (homedenture?) mix.<br /><br />There’s also something incredibly timely about this tale of allies turned enemies. While I was reading, the world’s leaders were discussing the ‘red line’ other countries shouldn’t cross and many were questioning the wisdom of drawing this kind of ‘line’ in the ground. Maybe because anyone who’s spent five minutes in a school playground knows it just makes everyone want to poke their toe over it. So it was interesting to see Derek Landy put the ‘wise’ in wisecrack and highlight the accidental arrogance of the Dead Men in their attempts to prevent war:<br /><br /><blockquote>“Right”, said Valkyrie. “So you’re basically hoping that your reputations will make them run away?”<br /><br />Skullduggery looked at her. “Well it just sounds silly when you say it out loud.”</blockquote><br /><br />And at a time when all you hear when you turn on the news are threats and bluster, there was something very relevant about Landy’s line:<br /><br /><blockquote>“When he’s backed into a corner, Basahalani will talk big and talk tough and all the time he’ll be crossing his fingers and hoping that you don’t stand your ground.”</blockquote><br /><br />But I know nothing puts you off a book quicker than the suspicion it might be ’educational’, so I should point out <i>The Last Stand of Dead Men</i> is also crazy, subversive and laugh out loud funny. You’ll get caught up and tossed about by the fast-pace and thrills of the battle scenes. Although, for me, the beauty of the book is it’s exploration of the stupidity of war and the horror of friends start attacking friends. Because, in the words of Derek Landy:<br /><br /><blockquote>“War is hell and it’s scary and how on earth is anyone supposed to know what side they’re on?”</blockquote><br /><br />Personally, I can’t wait for book nine to help me choose sides.<br /><br />Overall, another cracker from Derek Landy, and a great book to get people talking and (weirdly enough) laughing about the themes shaping global events<br /><br /><b>You can find this review, and many more, at Book Walrus <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://book-walrus.com/skulduggery-pleasant-last-stand-of-dead-men-derek-landy/">http://book-walrus.com/skulduggery-pl...</a></b><br /><br /><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/16123975.Last_Stand_of_Dead_Men__Skulduggery_Pleasant___8_" title="Last Stand of Dead Men (Skulduggery Pleasant, #8) by Derek Landy" rel="nofollow noopener">Last Stand of Dead Men</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="12468357608434540465" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/685912737?book_show_action=true">Aug 04, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Skyril" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Skyril" href="/user/show/14043443-skyril">Skyril</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer685912737" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14075651526617932165"><b>4.5</b><br/><br/>For anyone who is reading this review, I hope you have already read this book, as well as the previous seven, because there will be some spoilers.<br/><br/>First and foremost, this is the first <i>Skulduggery Pleasant</i> book that I have even considered giving a lower score than five.<br/><br/>Of course it was fantastic. Of course it was witty. Of course it was incredibly all-consuming.<br/><br/>However, Derek Landy seemed, for the first time, to kind of... be lazy about his rules and writing. <br/><br/>For instance, there are several ti</span>
  <span id="freeText14075651526617932165" style="display:none"><b>4.5</b><br /><br />For anyone who is reading this review, I hope you have already read this book, as well as the previous seven, because there will be some spoilers.<br /><br />First and foremost, this is the first <i>Skulduggery Pleasant</i> book that I have even considered giving a lower score than five.<br /><br />Of course it was fantastic. Of course it was witty. Of course it was incredibly all-consuming.<br /><br />However, Derek Landy seemed, for the first time, to kind of... be lazy about his rules and writing. <br /><br />For instance, there are several times when Fletcher teleports someone who, as far as I am aware, has never been teleported. For instance, Ajouga, the Bride of Blood Tears, or Bane and O'Callahan, and others.<br /><br />Another thing, the cloaking spheres? They didn't seem to have a time limit as they are meant to.<br />Odd.<br /><br />Lastly, the book was somewhat confusing. I blinked, went "What?," blinked again and couldn't figure a few things out. When Ravel gives his speech, and the shunter.... somehow... brings an alternate reality's Roarhaven to... well, Roarhaven. What? How? When did they build this? How? Who built it? No one knew about it? How did he shunt it over? I just do not get it. :/<br /><br />Unfortunately, there were a couple of other scenarios that confused me as well, but I am not going to get into them.<br />Basically, it was written less strictly and uniformly as usual.<br /><br />The goods still outweigh the bads, though. The characters are wonderful, stay true to their personalities, and develop. The plotline is brilliant. The ideas fantastic and believable. The fights? Amazing! I was just telling my mom how much I have grown to love the battles, not for the craziness or gore or death, but because no one cares about honor or dignity- only winning, in any way he possibly can. They fight dirty, and I love it.<br />It was a wonderful book, terrible, sad, but wonderful, which is absolutely to be expected of Derek Landy, and I <i>absolutely</i> enjoyed it.<br /><br />[And by the way, Derek Landy, I don't hate you as you thought I would. I don't know if you could do anything to make me hate you... Unless you kill off Skulduggery or Saracen. I love Saracen too much. DON'T DO IT!]</span>
  <a data-text-id="14075651526617932165" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

              <span id="reviewTextContainer541958544" class="readable"

<span id="freeTextContainer18104220910618117127">This book didn't start out much different from the other Skulduggery Pleasant books. It had the usual amounts of sass and sarcasm and narcissism and attitude, with a some violence and magic and weirdness thrown in there for hoots. It was fun to read. I laughed quite a bit and was constantly exclaiming about how much I loved it, even though there was a war going on. Despite the seriousness of it, everything was still okay.<br/><br/>Then, about half way through the book, there came a scene that changed ever</span>
  <span id="freeText18104220910618117127" style="display:none">This book didn't start out much different from the other Skulduggery Pleasant books. It had the usual amounts of sass and sarcasm and narcissism and attitude, with a some violence and magic and weirdness thrown in there for hoots. It was fun to read. I laughed quite a bit and was constantly exclaiming about how much I loved it, even though there was a war going on. Despite the seriousness of it, everything was still okay.<br /><br />Then, about half way through the book, there came a scene that changed everything. I'm sure those of you who have read the book know what scene I'm talking about. And things changed. Dramatically. The fun yet dark book that I started reading disappeared and was replaced by one that was different. It became so much harder to read. I began to turn every page with a new sense of dread, not knowing if any of the characters I had grown to love would live or die or have to make a very difficult choice that would ruin them for the rest of their life. The perspectives of each character grew worse and worse as the war continued and people fought and lost.<br /><br />I will certainly admit that this was a hard book to read. I've rarely encountered a book that has taken me by such surprise by how bleak and soul-ruining as LSODM. If this trend of spiraling into the depths of despair thing is going to continue, I think I'm really going to be afraid of reading the final book. It's going to be a heartbreaker, that's for sure.<br /><br />Derek Landy is a cruel, cruel author to kill so many people in the way he did. Some of those deaths were just awful. Even if they were once enemies of the main characters, they were still good people. They didn't deserve to die the way they did.<br /><br />And now, I have one last question: <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[ What secret does Dusk know about Valkyrie that she herself does not know? (Chapter 50, for reference)  <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span></span>

<span id="freeTextContainer9148006111493559448">WOW. WOW. WOW.<br/><br/>I don't want to spoil anything, but the strapline, "No one is safe'? Ain't that the truth. Some serious stuff (avoiding spoilers, see?) happens in this book. There's the usual death and destruction, plus some twists and revelations that I DID NOT see coming.<br/><br/>I can't believe that this is the second last time that I will ever pick up a Skulduggery Pleasant book for the first time... I think that I'll forever associate these books with my teenage years, and I am so, so happy to have gr</span>
  <span id="freeText9148006111493559448" style="display:none">WOW. WOW. WOW.<br /><br />I don't want to spoil anything, but the strapline, "No one is safe'? Ain't that the truth. Some serious stuff (avoiding spoilers, see?) happens in this book. There's the usual death and destruction, plus some twists and revelations that I DID NOT see coming.<br /><br />I can't believe that this is the second last time that I will ever pick up a Skulduggery Pleasant book for the first time... I think that I'll forever associate these books with my teenage years, and I am so, so happy to have grown up reading them. I've completely fallen in love with these characters, and this book just continues that on a massive scale. For me, the previous book, Kingdom of the Wicked, wasn't the best of the series, but I was completely astounded by Last Stand of Dead Men. I'm not sure, but I think this is my favourite SP book yet.<br /><br />It was a bit emotionally taxing, this one. At least more so than the others. There's the same humour that exists in all of the books, but this one's darker, and very, very, very enthralling. I read it in less than 24 hours, and when I was finished, I just sat there and stared at the book for a while, trying to process everything that had happened. I'm still recovering, I think. I can't really say anything about the plot, except that some MAJORLY unexpected things happen. There are new characters, old characters and some serious plot developments.<br /><br />And that cover. Yikes.<br /><br />Now all I have to do is wait another year for the next (and last...) book to come out. I think that I might expire from impatience in that time.</span>

<div id="review_621003449" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">

    <a title="Jessica (aus.fangirl.reads)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/14748186-jessica-aus-fangirl-reads"><img alt="Jessica (aus.fangirl.reads)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1502893074p2/14748186.jpg" /></a>

        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780007489213" href="/book/show/17869233-last-stand-of-dead-men">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14748186-jessica-aus-fangirl-reads?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>,

              <span id="reviewTextContainer621003449" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11915882922425767350">No matter how prepared I was for this book it still managed to rip my heart out and throw it at my own face! <br/>This book is full of action and emotions, while still having time to make you laugh. In the middle of a war you find yourself laughing at something one of the Dead Men has said or thought. Only certain authors can have you laughing while there is a war going on in the background and Derek does an amazing job.<br/><br/>One of my favourite things about this book is after so much mentioning, we finall</span>
  <span id="freeText11915882922425767350" style="display:none">No matter how prepared I was for this book it still managed to rip my heart out and throw it at my own face! <br />This book is full of action and emotions, while still having time to make you laugh. In the middle of a war you find yourself laughing at something one of the Dead Men has said or thought. Only certain authors can have you laughing while there is a war going on in the background and Derek does an amazing job.<br /><br />One of my favourite things about this book is after so much mentioning, we finally get the full Dead Men back together and it is magnificent to see them go off on missions together and just be sassy with one another.<br /><br /><b>"Strike from the shadows, disappear into darkness"</b> -The Dead Men Motto<br /><br />Bring on Dying of the Light! </span>
  <a data-text-id="11915882922425767350" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer704030499" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8539973875997378902">You know what sucks the most about this book? That I have to wait a year, a YEAR for the next one! <br/><br/>I think this is the funniest in the series. It is also probably the scariest and the outlook is definitely the most dire for our Skulduggery and his team. I am very mad at Derek Landy about a few things, but I'm not going to spoil it for the rest of you - you will see what I mean when you get there. <br/><br/>I wish more adult books would read like this. </span>

          </span>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('wAGyLFBrj3+BGuyEvTKjbMkfCT+Ts0RxJJm4o/WF6K+fMS8O/RjdZ4G80gk9DMqBXEX8ALGGUtUTGjy6tZB7Sg==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('MtNKc0Am7c7pWf4sV8yWkYO+HxRsImV9WYr01Pgodsht49dR7VW/1un/wKHX8v98FuTqK04Xc9luCXDNuD3lLQ==')})
  }

But she is not the only customer; a cocky mage and a drastically overworked yet underpaid sage become regulars as well.\n\nThe knight brings trouble to the diner at times, but Dennis’s cooking skills and beloved butcher knives cut through trouble and hunger alike!\n\nThus begins the legend of Dennis and his diner, the talk of the town!<\/span>\n  <a data-text-id=\"6757559652099527223\" href=\"#\" <div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer11138808233102183499">Derek Landy is an Irish writer and screenwriter. In addition to the bestselling children's/YA series of <i>Skulduggery Pleasant</i> books, a supernatural mystery series starring Skulduggery Pleasant, a skeleton detective, and Valkyrie Cain, a young female magician, he has written two screenplays that have been made into films: the IFTA award winning "Dead Bodies" and the IFTA nominated "Boy Eats Girl". L</span>
  <span id="freeText11138808233102183499" style="display:none">Derek Landy is an Irish writer and screenwriter. In addition to the bestselling children's/YA series of <i>Skulduggery Pleasant</i> books, a supernatural mystery series starring Skulduggery Pleasant, a skeleton detective, and Valkyrie Cain, a young female magician, he has written two screenplays that have been made into films: the IFTA award winning "Dead Bodies" and the IFTA nominated "Boy Eats Girl". Landy himself was nominated for an IFTA for Best Script. <br /><br />He doesn’t like to brag about all the awards he’s won, such as the Irish Book of the Decade, or the Red House in the UK, or all the other awards that he humbly displays on his mantelpiece. He is also far too modest to mention things like the first book being a Publisher’s Weekly Best Book of the Year, but would like to extend an invitation to Oprah to pop around one day for tea, in thanks for selecting his book for the Oprah’s Book Club Kids Reading List. <br /><br />Derek plays too many video games, reads too many comics, and watches too many movies. He lives in Ireland with too many cats. Occasionally he talks to real people, but only when he absolutely has to.</span>
